Local News

Japanese Goods and Essential Raw Materials

Deliberations on Levy of Funds

Principle Approved by Executive Committee Meeting

Detailed Measures Being Drafted by Committee

The Anti-Japanese Association has repeatedly discussed Japanese industrial raw materials and essential goods in the Design Committee and the Executive Committee meetings. It was felt that a blanket boycott was impossible. Factories in need should report to the meeting, await investigation, and set regulations. Recently, various guilds, such as the cotton cloth industry, have written to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, advocating for the levy of industrial raw materials and essential goods as an industrial fund to prepare for the establishment of factories, which has attracted the attention of the Anti-Japanese Association. It is reported that the Anti-Japanese Association is considering the levy of funds. The news is recorded as follows:

Method for Levying Funds - At 5 p.m. the day before yesterday, the Anti-Japanese Association held an executive committee meeting. The issue of levying an industrial fund was discussed in detail. Members present included Tao Baichuan, Zhang Honghai, Lu Xingzhuang, Hou Dachun, Wang Yansong, Xi Yushu, Wang Hanliang, Yan E'sheng, Hu Fengxiang, Zheng Chengqing, Tang Junsheng, and others. As a result, the principle of levying an industrial fund was approved by vote. However, (1) the method of levy and (2) the method of preservation should be extremely meticulous and thorough. This fund should absolutely not be used for other purposes until a sufficient amount is available to establish factories. Detailed rules were drawn up by Wang Yansong, Zheng Chengqing, Hu Fengxiang, Lu Xingzhuang, and Yan E'sheng as drafting committee members, with Zheng Chengqing as the convener. It is said that this drafting meeting will be held soon.

Separate Measures for Fine Yarn - The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Dyeing and Weaving Federation has resolved to levy a fine yarn factory fund on fine yarn produced by Japanese factories. On the one hand, members of the industry will subscribe for 250,000 yuan to show their support. This case was also discussed by the Executive Committee of the Anti-Japanese Association, which resolved to submit it to the Design Committee for further study in order to decide on its handling. At the same time, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce also replied to the Jiangyin County Chamber of Commerce regarding the fine yarn issue, stating that: "We are writing to inform you that we received your letter on the 7th of this month, stating that the fine yarn produced by Chinese yarn factories is very small and insufficient. Therefore, previous efforts to store goods have set separate measures to maintain domestic industry. Please forward this letter to the Anti-Japanese Association to seek relief and separate handling. This matter has been resolved by the fourth Executive Committee meeting of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee in our city. Regarding industrial raw materials and daily necessities that cannot be replaced in fact, standards should first be established. Our Association will send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to promptly establish a Research Committee on Resisting Japanese Goods to study and establish standards in detail, and submit them to our Association for reference, etc. Therefore, the method of maintaining industrial raw materials is being considered by the Anti-Japanese Association, and there is no need to send another letter. The organization of our Chamber's Research Committee on Resisting Japanese Goods will also be completed soon. We are writing to inform you accordingly, and please check and notify us."

Anti-Japanese Association and Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Registration of Japanese Goods Completed

Total of 1,500 Registration Forms Received

Continued Seizure of Goods in Various Districts of the City (North, South, East, and West)

The Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee and the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce have separately registered Japanese goods, both of which ended on the 6th of this month. Now that the deadline has passed, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has sent all registration forms to the Anti-Japanese Association. The handling of the two associations is recorded as follows:

Registrations by the Anti-Japanese Association - The Registration Section of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee has received a total of 700 Japanese goods registration forms. The section is now sorting the forms by type of goods and sending them to the Investigation Section for investigation. Once the investigation is completed and the items match, the association will stamp each item of goods, allowing them to be sold. However, because there are so many registered goods, the investigation cannot be completed immediately. In addition to the resolution by the Standing Committee to have the Investigation Section speed up their work, the investigation will be conducted in order of registration.

Registrations by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce - The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously resolved at a temporary members' meeting that the registration matters of factories and shops that purchase and store Japanese goods and are members of the Chamber's trade associations or shop members should be handled by the Chamber. Once the registration deadline has passed, the Chamber will submit the registration forms to the Anti-Japanese Association for review and certification. As of the 6th of this month, a total of 4,116 registration forms have been issued, with three copies each. A total of 849 copies have been completed and submitted to the Chamber. The number of reports from various industry associations and the Pudong, Wusong, and Jiangwan branch offices are listed separately: (1) Pudong 44 copies, (2) Wusong 57 copies, (3) Electrical Industry 48 copies, (4) Hardware Industry 21 copies, (5) Rubber Products Industry 22 copies, (6) Floral Industry 13 copies, (7) Watch Industry 56 copies, (8) Chinese and Western Furniture Industry 67 copies, (9) Southern Goods Industry 136 copies, (10) Cotton Cloth Industry 53 copies, (11) Timber Industry 44 copies, (12) Western Paint Industry 26 copies, (13) Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry 24 copies, (14) Porcelain Industry 5 copies, (15) Transportation Industry 6 copies, (16) Restaurant Industry 8 copies, (17) Ivory and Bone Products Industry 11 copies, (18) Southern and Northern Goods Exchange Industry 18 copies, (19) Department Store Industry 10 copies, (20) Mercerized Cotton Paper Industry 30 copies, (21) Rubber, Hardware, and Vehicle Parts Industry 9 copies, (22) Fresh Fish Industry 6 copies, (23) Seafood and Sundries Industry 20 copies, (24) Book Industry 8 copies, (25) Chinese Soap Industry 6 copies, (26) Paper Industry 17 copies, (27) Sugar Industry 9 copies, (28) Shoe Industry 3 copies, (29) Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Food Industry 4 copies, (30) Silk and Satin Industry 2 copies, (31) Chinese Candle Industry 2 copies, (32) Tobacco Exchange Industry 2 copies, (33) Cosmetics Industry 2 copies, (34) Medicinal Materials Industry 25 copies, (35) Chinese Grains, Oil, and Cake Industry 1 copy, (36) Transit and Customs Brokerage Industry 1 copy, (37) Yarn Industry 1 copy, (38) Iron Industry 1 copy, (39) Flour Mill Industry 1 copy, (40) Sauce Garden Industry 1 copy, (41) Letterpress Printing Industry 1 copy, (42) Gunny Sack Industry 1 copy, (43) Northern Goods Industry 1 copy, (44) Auction Industry 1 copy, (45) Sanyou Electric Company 1 copy, (46) Chinese Auction House 1 copy, (47) Jiangwan Branch Office 33 copies. In total, 45 industry association members and 2 shop members have come to register Japanese goods.

Goods Ordered Are Not Allowed to Be Registered - The Municipal Chamber of Commerce replied to the Hardware Trade Association that orders cannot be registered, stating that: "We are writing to inform you that we received your letter on the 7th of this month, requesting us to discuss with the Anti-Japanese Association about registering goods that have been ordered but not yet shipped. After investigation, the Anti-Japanese Association's registration of Japanese goods, although divided into two methods before the 14th and before the 24th, refers to those who have paid for and stored the goods. Goods that have been ordered but not yet arrived are not included in the registration. It is really inappropriate to follow your request to forward the itemized list to the Association for registration. As for the goods for which a deposit has been paid but the Japanese factory refuses to refund, the Chinese Soap Industry Trade Association has previously inquired about the method, which has been forwarded to the Anti-Japanese Association and is still awaiting a reply. The situation in your letter is roughly the same as that of the Soap Industry. Your association can follow it in the future if there is a commercial solution."

Continued Seizure of Japanese Goods - The Inspection Section of the Anti-Japanese Association continues to announce the following seizures of Japanese goods as of August 6: (1) August 1, Yongxing Silk Factory in Zhabei seized one bundle of Japanese yarn, a total of ten pieces; (2) August 2, two boats of sugar at Caojiadu, five pieces of cloth from Huamei Company at the South Station, thirteen reams of paper from Puye Company, five pieces of white paper from Jiuji, two pieces of Taolin paper, one package of Feng Yunsheng mosquito coils, seven Zhengqin Qin Zheng Qin Zheng Qin Qin from Wei Shun Ji in one piece, and eight bales of thread from Sanxin Company; (3) August 3, one piece of Kaiyang and one piece of Xiangjun from Tongfengxiang at Caojiadu in West Shanghai, 1,000 bags of rice sold to Taichangxiang by Yongda Company in Pudong, two bags of shark fins from Zhenda Company at the North Station in Zhabei, 199 pieces of colored clothing at Rihui Port, over 400 pieces of film from Xielong Match Hardboard Company, one bundle of thermos bottles from Shen Da Company, four pieces of Fuji paper, six reams of paper from Yubenliang Company; (4) August 4, 275 pieces of yarn and 85 pieces of foreign cloth at Huatong Wharf in Pudong, and four small packages of red thread from Huatong Warehouse; (5) August 5, one Zhengqin Qin Zheng Qin Zheng Qin Qin Qin Qin Zheng Qin Zhengqin from Nanyang Socks Factory in Caojiadu, one Zhengqin Qin Zheng Qin Zhengqin from Yufeng, one piece of Ren from Taichang Shipping Bureau, two dozen thermos bottles from Tianshunsheng at the 16th Pier, one box of flashlights from Dehe, one box of cloth from Huitai, two boxes of scarves from Yongli, and two pairs of thin cloth from Yongfeng; (6) August 6, ten bundles of white pine wood from Yongchang Wood Company in Wujiaochang.

Foreign Communists

Noulens Couple Judged

Escorted to Garrison Headquarters for Trial

On June 15 of this year, the Political Department of the Public Concession's Bureau of Works learned that the Third International had sent a top-level Communist member to establish a secret organization in the Concession to direct red bandits throughout China and promote domestic turmoil. They raided the organization at No. 49 Sichuan Road, Nanjing Road, and seized 600 important documents from various countries. The leader of the party, a Westerner named Noulens (alias Vanderuyssu, 37 years old) and his wife, Notte (alias Vandercruysu.s, 37 years old), were arrested and sent to the Second Branch of the High Court. They were interrogated several times behind closed doors. At 9:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, Song Yuan, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division of the High Court, along with Judges Ye and Gao, resumed the interrogation. The Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing also telegraphed the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to send a letter to the High Court requesting their transfer. Therefore, yesterday morning, Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor of the Garrison Headquarters, arrived in court to state the reasons for requesting the transfer. The defendants also hired a lawyer to defend them, stating that the defendants were Swiss citizens and should be managed by the Swiss government. The court ruled that the two defendants should be handed over to the Garrison Headquarters for handling the case. Upon hearing the verdict, the defendants declared their appeal. The court then ruled that the appeal in this case was not allowed and adjourned the court at 3:30 p.m.

Another report stated that the Westerners, the Vanderuyssu couple, were charged with propagating communism. After repeated court hearings by the Second Branch of the High Court, they were ordered to be handed over to the Garrison Headquarters for trial the day before yesterday. Van was arrested on June 15 at No. 235 Sichuan Road. A bunch of keys was found on his person, which matched the room at No. 49 Nanjing Road. The room was subsequently searched and a large number of communist propaganda materials were seized. Van's wife was arrested at the same location and returned to the police station. Van claimed to be a Belgian national, but the Belgian Consul General did not recognize him. He was then sent to the Second Branch of the High Court for trial. During the continued trial the day before yesterday, Van again claimed to be Swiss, originally named Blye, and listed the surnames of his parents. When questioned by the representative of the Swiss Consulate General, he said that although there was such a surname in Switzerland, it was not known whether it was the person himself and further investigation was needed. The judge then stated that the defendant had failed to produce any physical or testimonial evidence sufficient to prove Swiss citizenship, and ordered him to be handed over to the Garrison Headquarters for trial. The defendant's lawyer wanted to appeal, but the judge said that an appeal was not allowed according to regulations and did not grant his request. Van's wife was the one who went on a hunger strike in the Xiamen Road West Prison for a week.

Swiss Protection

Repercussions of the Arrested Communist Leader

The various levels of party headquarters in this city are extremely indignant about the Swiss Consul's protection of communists in Shanghai. The positions of the party headquarters in the four districts, the three sub-branches in the ninth district, the five sub-branches in the ninth district, and the six sub-branches in the second district on this case are as follows:

Party Headquarters in the Fourth District - Noulens and his wife, the leaders of the Communist Party's Eastern Department, were arrested in the Public Concession of Shanghai on June 16. Hundreds of important reactionary evidence were seized on the spot, the most of which were related to plans to command the Red Army in combat. When Noulens was arrested, he claimed to be of Belgian nationality, and his wife claimed to be of French nationality. After investigation, it was found that the two criminals had no nationality. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters then sent a letter requesting their transfer. The criminals, knowing that they could not escape punishment, bribed the Swiss Consul in Shanghai to admit that the criminals were Swiss citizens on the 8th of this month. The Presiding Judge Song of the Second Branch of the Special District Court then asked the Swiss representative to present evidence of nationality, but nothing was obtained. Based on this, it is clear that the Swiss Consul accepted a bribe and protected the Communist leaders, disregarding international relations, which is extremely abhorrent. Yesterday, the party headquarters in the fourth district of this city sent a letter warning that if they dared to defend the criminals again, they would be expelled from the country.

Five Sub-Branches in the Ninth District - The sub-branch requested permission from its superiors to convene a general assembly of citizens in Shanghai to discuss severing diplomatic relations with Switzerland for the Swiss Consul's protection of Communist leaders such as Noulens. The document stated: "Noulens and his wife, the leaders of the Communist Party's Third International, are stationed in China and specialize in directing the Chinese Communist Party in Hunan, Hubei, Fujian, Jiangxi, and other provinces to engage in murder and arson. The criminals were arrested in the Public Concession on July 16, and a large number of important Communist documents, totaling over 600, were seized. However, the nationality of the criminals was repeatedly investigated by the police station and the court before it was learned that the criminals were foreigners without nationality. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters requested extradition from the Second Branch of the Special Court. The criminals did not hesitate to bribe the Swiss Consul with a large sum of money. A representative was sent to court on the 8th of this month to admit that the criminals were Swiss citizens. Because there was no evidence, Presiding Judge Song rejected the request and allowed the Garrison Headquarters to extradite them. Unexpectedly, the Swiss Consul, intoxicated by money and willing to harm our 400 million compatriots in China, did not suppress the criminals who brutally murdered unarmed victims in Hunan, Hubei, Fujian, and Jiangxi provinces, but dared to protect them. Therefore, we specifically request that superiors allow a general assembly of citizens in Shanghai to be convened to discuss severing diplomatic relations with Switzerland."

Three Sub-Branches in the Ninth District - The sub-branch issued a declaration warning the Swiss Consul in Shanghai against protecting Communists, stating: "Noulens and his wife, the leaders of the Communist Party's Eastern Department, were arrested in the Public Concession and hundreds of important pieces of evidence were seized, including plans to command the Red Army in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei, and methods for using poison gas. After the criminals were arrested, they claimed to be Belgian, and his wife claimed to be French. After the authorities inquired with Belgium and France, there was no such person. The criminals are the leaders of the Red Army who harm China, and have held important positions in the Communist bandits in Jiangxi Province. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters sent a letter requesting their extradition. The criminals knew that their crimes could not be concealed, so they came up with a far-fetched idea and did not hesitate to bribe the Swiss Consul to come out and protect them. On the 8th of this month, a representative was sent to the court to request extradition and to be handled by the Swiss Consul. Presiding Judge Song found that the criminals had not registered in Switzerland and had no passports, and refused to allow the extradition. According to the previous situation, it is clear that the Swiss Consul is protecting Communists, which is beyond doubt. However, our country is currently carrying out a major campaign to suppress the Reds. The Swiss Consul dares to defy the world and become a public enemy of the entire nation. If he does not repent and intends to interfere again, we will rise up and resist. We hereby declare."

Six Sub-Branches in the Second District - "The disaster of the Communist Party is worse than water and fire, and all countries in the world regard them as public enemies. This time, Noulens and his wife, the leaders of the Communist Party's Eastern Department, were arrested and found to have no nationality. However, the Swiss Consul actually recognized the criminals as Swiss citizens and requested their extradition. The Presiding Judge Song of the Second Branch of the Special District Court then asked the Consul's representative to present evidence, but the extradition was refused because there was no evidence. The criminals had not registered in Switzerland and had no passports, and were clearly stateless. According to international law, anyone who commits a crime in a place without nationality should be handled by the local authorities. After the criminals were arrested, the Consul disregarded international law and dared to come out and protect the Communists, defying the world. All our comrades should fight for it. The comrades of this sub-branch vow to be the government's backup and sever diplomatic relations with that country. We hereby declare."

The China Bookstore Resumes Business Today

Quietly Awaiting Official Review According to the Law

The Labor Community Will Hold a Meeting Today to Offer Assistance

Following the general factory of the China Bookstore telegraphing its temporary closure, the Bureau of Social Affairs immediately ordered its resumption. After a resolution by the bookstore’s board of directors, it will comply with the order and resume operations today, quietly awaiting review. The labor union has already submitted its demands regarding compensation and benefits. The local labor community will hold a meeting today to discuss assistance. The various developments of yesterday are recorded below:

Notice of Reopening: The China Bookstore issued a notice that it would resume normal operations starting today, in compliance with orders. On the sixth of this month, the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union sent a letter requesting an early dismissal of one and a half hours on the afternoon of the seventh for a meeting. Our bookstore responded with a letter at 10:00 AM on the seventh, inquiring about the scope. The union replied with a letter, and then at 3:00 PM, a large group of people came to the bookstore, blocked the front and back doors of the general factory, and forcibly drove employees from their workplaces to hold a meeting in an open space. These events were reported in a telegram on the evening of the seventh. On the eighth, representatives from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce came to investigate and verify the state of chaos and losses. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs instructed that normal operations must resume tomorrow, quietly awaiting review by the bureau. Our bookstore immediately convened a board meeting and decided that, starting from Monday, the tenth of this month, normal operations would resume. This notice is hereby issued for public awareness.

The Union's Attitude: Chen Xuanren, the executive director of the Municipal Publishing Industry Union, told a reporter from the New Voice News Agency yesterday that the China Bookstore's recent shutdown and its attempts to disguise the situation were the most clumsy attempts to undermine the labor movement. Therefore, our union takes a dim view of the bookstore's closure, as we know that it is not a direct response to the union, but rather a tactic to delay improving the terms of employment. Our union has seen through their strategy and has decided to let the closure take its course while focusing on negotiating for better terms of employment, seeking a resolution within three days. If the bookstore can fully understand the true meaning of labor-management cooperation, it should not lead to unexpected disputes. Otherwise, even if the bookstore is determined to close for three months, our union is prepared and can handle it with ease. Their efforts will only prove to be futile.

Union Meeting: More than twenty labor unions, including municipal postal, utilities, letterpress printing, sauce, and cigarette industries, have initiated a representative assembly to assist the publishing industry, sending a notice to all labor unions stating: The China Bookstore branch of the Publishing Industry Union formally established its branch office on August 8, with representatives from party and government agencies attending to provide guidance. The meeting was orderly. However, the bookstore's management has resorted to the base and cunning tactics of the past, disrupting the labor movement by unilaterally suspending operations to assert its dominance. Our unions believe that this action by the China Bookstore's management not only affects the livelihoods of the bookstore's workers but also poses a threat to the entire labor movement. If it is not severely punished, the entire labor movement will be destroyed. We are all in the same boat and cannot shirk our responsibility. We have scheduled a joint meeting at the Postal Workers' Union at 3:00 PM on August 10 to discuss countermeasures. We hope that you will send representatives to attend on time.

Donations for Assistance: The Commerce Press branch of the Publishing Industry Union held a joint meeting of executives and group leaders at 4:00 PM yesterday to discuss the China Bookstore's management's oppression of labor. It was decided that, in addition to unanimously supporting the Publishing Industry Union, all members, more than forty people, would voluntarily donate one day's wages to help the China Bookstore's employees.

Nationwide

Preparations for the National Road and Municipal Exhibition

A Three-Week Exhibition Scheduled to be Held in Shanghai

Chinese and Western Experts and Celebrities Participating in the Design

Exhibits from Provinces and Cities Across the Country Have Been Shipped

A Grand Scale, Unprecedented

The China National Roads Construction Association has been established for ten years. This time, it is preparing to hold a Road and Municipal Exhibition to commemorate this anniversary and to promote the construction of new roads and highways in various provinces, reward the development of municipal and public buildings, and promote the construction of modern municipal and highway administration. As the opening date of the conference is approaching, a summary of the general plan of the conference and the current preparations is recorded on the left.

Venue Location and Buildings: The exhibition venue is located on Avenue Petain in the French Concession of Shanghai, covering an area of ​​sixty to seventy acres. The construction of the buildings has already begun and will generally adopt a Chinese style. The entrances are lined up, with ample display space, allocated according to grade and type, and the layout is very detailed.

Exhibition Content and Facilities: The venue has a theater attached to it, which can accommodate one thousand people. The facilities are as complete as possible. Exhibitors and the National Roads Association can hold speeches and masquerade performances here, as well as show industrial films. There are speeches on road construction projects, municipal management design, and various entertainment programs to entertain official and commercial representatives and visitors. The venue also has a dance floor, reception room, Chinese and Western restaurants to facilitate all the daily needs of the attendees.

Entertainment Items and Participating Celebrities: The entertainment program is very rich. The exhibition is scheduled for three weeks. Every day from 3:00 PM to 6:00 PM, there are performances of film, martial arts, and various miscellaneous items. The evening entertainment program is different every week. The first week is Western-style music, dance entertainment, etc. The second week is Peking opera and various cameos. Celebrities such as Wang Xiaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Du Yuesheng, and Zhang Xiaolin are willing to participate enthusiastically and make appearances, adding a lot of color to the conference. The third week has Chinese and Western dramas, responsible for the actresses Wang Lianqing (daughter of Mr. Wang Xiaolai), Yu Xiuyun (granddaughter of Mr. Yu Qiaqing), etc. The dance floor is held as usual every night. It is an open-air style and holds various competitions in costumes and dance skills, and prepares valuable gifts to attract the interest of the participants.

Conference Schedule and Staff: The conference is scheduled for three weeks, from September 12 (Saturday) to October 2 (Friday) of this year. Participants include representatives from the National Government, various ministries and committees, and provinces and cities, construction department heads, highway bureau directors, engineering consultants, as well as road engineers, road builders, and manufacturers related to road vehicles at home and abroad. The responsible staff includes Chairman Wang Zhengting, Vice Chairman Kong Xiangxi, initiators Xu Shiying, Xu Yuan, Yuan Ludeng, Zhao Xien, Ouyang Rongzhi, Zheng Hongnian, Zhu Shaoping, Qian Yongming, Rong Zongjing, and accounting director Yin Ruli, Secretary Dong Ping Wu Kaisheng, and Director-General Wu Shan. The Director-General of the exhibition is Yang Nianzu, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, Chairman Zhao Xien, Cao Yunxiang, Vice Chairman Shi Fangnan, Luo Jiai, Hua Secretary Zheng Xitao, Western Secretary Jin Shibo, Director of the Finance Section Zhu Boquan, Director of the Propaganda Section Shi Liangcai, Deputy Director Wang Yingbin, Director of the Display Section Luo Jiai, Director of the Collection Section Shi Fangnan, and Director of the Entertainment Section Wang Xiaolai. With Chinese and Western celebrities gathered together, working together, its success can be predicted.

The Richness of the Collection of Exhibits: The types of exhibits are numerous, and concrete models related to road construction machinery and vehicles are all collected. They are divided into categories, forming a grand view. Exhibits from provinces across the country have been shipped one after another. It is said that the exhibits shipped by the Hankou Municipal Engineering Bureau alone have reached twenty-one large boxes. If combined with the exhibits from other provinces and cities, its prosperity and splendor can be imagined.

Manufacturers Participating in the Exhibition: It is said that manufacturers participating in the exhibition are also very enthusiastic. Major well-known British, American, German, and French companies in Shanghai, such as Ford Motor Factory and Merton Motor Company, have jointly purchased more than eight display locations. General Motors, Metronome Foreign Firm, Kong Shitianxiang Foreign Firm, Badehual Foreign Firm, Liwei Automobile Bank, Longfei Automobile Bank, Lihua Foreign Firm, Mobil, Asia, Texaco, Guangyu, Youlian, and other gasoline banks, Anli Foreign Firm, Taikang Company, Wheeler Company, Jinshan Iron Factory, Chanson Foreign Firm, Qianxin Foreign Firm, Yichang Foreign Firm, and Gumin Foreign Firm have all booked large locations to display new and exciting exhibits.

Admission Tickets with Valuable Gifts: The conference is held in Shanghai, where land and water transportation is very convenient. Representatives, exhibitors, and visitors attending the conference can all get special comfort and pleasure. Therefore, it will surely become an unprecedented grand event in the history of international exhibitions. Various measures and equipment are supported economically and spiritually by the central authorities, party authorities in provinces and cities, and the financial, industrial, and educational circles across the country. It is estimated that at least 150 Chinese representatives and at least 50 foreign representatives will attend. During the three weeks of the conference, at least 100,000 people from all parts of China and other countries are expected to visit. The preparatory office has printed 100,000 admission tickets, each selling for one yuan. It is said that more than 10,000 tickets have been sold in the past few days. The ticket face also has prizes. The first prize is a Picard sedan worth 10,000 yuan, the second prize is a valuable Hodge car, the third prize is a Small Morris sedan, and there are many other small prizes, also worth more than 10,000 yuan. In addition to sightseeing, there are also prizes to be won, which is enough to arouse the interest of entrants.

It is found that China's road construction had only 1,500 miles in the tenth year of the Republic of China, but as of this year, it has 35,000 miles. In ten years, it has increased more than twenty times. The association’s promotion has indeed accounted for a large part. The twenty-first year of the Republic of China will usher in a new era of road construction. Therefore, it is firmly believed that the general public will enthusiastically participate in this unprecedented event, supporting the old and leading the young. It is expected that on the opening day, representatives from the north and south will come from more than twenty provinces across the country, and it will be a scene of tens of thousands of people leaving their homes and horses and carriages like clouds, presenting an unprecedented grand scene on the deserted Avenue Petain.

Coal Industry

Please Convene a National Coal Mine Merchants Conference

To Determine National Coal Policy

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association yesterday presented to the Executive Yuan, stating: In order to solve the national coal plan, please convene a conference. In recent years, our coal and coke merchants have been suffering due to the poor environment, while foreign coal has taken the opportunity to move in and gradually dominate transportation and sales, controlling the key to manipulation. The life of our country's transportation and industry has already been placed in the hands of foreign coal. As for the leakage of economic benefits, it is becoming more and more serious, and it is unbearable to recall. I respectfully read the Premier's industrial plan, in which the use of coal and the plugging of leaks are already in the eyes of all our citizens who can read. The appeals of the Shanghai coal merchants have also long been heard by the general public. However, since the establishment of the National Government five years ago, no far-sighted plan or fact of development has been made for this major coal mining issue. Therefore, the Shanghai coal merchants are unwilling to remain silent and offer their humble opinions. It is found that the Ministry of Industry previously held an industrial conference. Now, please follow the example to determine the national coal policy. However, coal merchants and miners have a close relationship with railway transportation. I respectfully request your Yuan to order the three ministries of industry, transportation, and railway to jointly convene a national conference of coal merchants and miners to plan, develop, and transport and sell national coal, in order to plug leaks and enrich the country. The above-mentioned proposals are respectfully requested to be adopted and implemented by your Yuan. The Shanghai coal merchants will do their best to serve the country. I respectfully present this to the Executive Yuan of the National Government.

Minutes of the Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors of the Lawyers Association

85th Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 85th joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members at 10:00 AM yesterday (Sunday). The committee members present were Li Shirui, Huang Han, Liu Zuwang, Zhang Feixiong, Lu Shaozong, Zhao Zuwei, Tang Yingsong, Zhao Yuhuang, Lu Jianai, Shen Junru, Tan Yigong, Wen Chao, Chen Zemin, Zhang Enhan, and Shan Yuhua. The investigation report will be forwarded to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Party Department for information. (5) The Hangxian Lawyers Association forwarded Lawyer Tang Zhang's reply to the Shanghai Association's letter prohibiting him from practicing in Shanghai. It was resolved to forward it to Member Cao Lin for information. (8) A prisoner in Dongyang County, Shaoxing, Zhejiang, sent a letter requesting assistance in petitioning the National Government for amnesty. It was resolved to file it for future reference. Please ask the local Fifth District Second Branch to assist in the execution, but the branch not only does not assist but also obstructs the execution and interferes with the judiciary outside the law. Please review and correct it. It was resolved to forward it to the Shanghai District Court and request that civil execution cases be strictly enforced. It was resolved to recommend that Committee Members Shan Yuhua and Lu Jianai investigate before reviewing it. (11) Wu Zhongle sent a letter reporting that Lawyer Yi Zhendong owed rent and moved privately, and demanded rent increases. Please uphold justice. It was resolved to reply to Wu Zhongle that if there is evidence of rent arrears, he can handle it according to law. (12) Committee Member Wen Chao proposed opinions on revising the articles of association. It was resolved to open a special committee to discuss it. (13) Please approve the association's repair expenses. It was resolved that repairs should be carried out and handed over to the Standing Committee for review. It was resolved to hand it over to the Standing Committee for review. The meeting adjourned at 2:00 PM.

Liuhe Flood Relief Association Begging Telegram

To the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the Chinese Jisheng Association, the Red Cross Society, the National Flood Relief Association, the Jiangsu Relief Committee, the Lianyi Charity Society, various charity halls, all philanthropists, fathers and elders across the country, and all newspapers: Heaven has punished us in Liuhe. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, after a great drought that turned the entire territory into red land, we have been hit by a flood unseen in more than eighty years. The county is bordered by mountains in the northwest near Anhui and by the river in the southeast. The Chu River runs through the middle, flowing from west to east, and is the only drainage channel. Its capacity is originally narrow and has been silted up due to disrepair. Suddenly, the river rose in the last month and continued for more than ten days, day and night, with heavy rain like pouring water. Mountain floods poured down, and the river tide rose again, causing overflowing in all directions. Ninety-nine percent of the dikes, fields, and farmlands on the east, west, and south sides were breached and completely submerged. The lower-lying farmlands were also affected by the disaster as much as the diked fields. When the flood was at its highest, the drowned population, livestock, and grain (estimated at hundreds of thousands of stones) and the materials of collapsed houses (estimated at more than 30,000) were swept downstream, a sight that was frightening. According to rough estimates, the total area of ​​disaster-stricken farmland is more than 400,000 mu, and more than 300 large and small dikes were broken and submerged, with countless breaches, exceeding half of the total farmland in the county. The remaining small number of farmlands that were least affected were also more than half-affected. More than 100,000 people are displaced, without shelter or livelihood. The direct and indirect losses to the entire county's 360,000 people are unavoidable. Looking up, everything has become a lake. Smoke has stopped, and there is no sound of chickens and dogs. Patrol boats observe that on the small mounds and hills, disaster victims gather like flies and ants, calling out in the wilderness. The city is several feet deep in water. When entering and exiting the city gates, boatmen must crawl to avoid hitting obstacles. According to the old farmers, the flood is worse than that of the late Qing Daoguang years. The surviving people, who have just suffered from a rare drought, have been hit by this disaster again, and their lives are unbearable. Currently, the flood has not receded, and even if it does recede slightly, it will be extremely slow. Counting the seasons, there is no possibility of replanting autumn grain. The hope for the future is gone, and it is difficult to prolong the current breath. In addition to trying our best to scrape together and temporarily prepare coarse grains locally and distribute them selectively to extend their lives, the county is small and the people are poor, the disaster is heavy, and the area is wide. It is difficult to support the situation even for a moment. The situation is extremely critical. We appeal to all charitable organizations and philanthropists to treat everyone equally, send personnel to the county day and night with donations to provide emergency relief, so that the dying can be spared for a moment and struggle again. We are ready to wait for your urgent orders. The Liuhe County Flood Relief Committee kowtows.

Dongtai Compatriots Discuss Emergency Relief

Dongtai compatriots in Shanghai received a telegram from the Dongtai County Party, Business, Agriculture, and Education groups, stating that the three dams of Gaoyou were opened at the same time, and the entire county was turned into a swamp. Houses and property were washed away, and the lives of 1.3 million people were in critical danger. We hope to quickly ask various relief associations to release emergency relief and continue to send details by letter. Therefore, an emergency meeting was held at the Youth Association last night. Those who attended included Xia Hucen, Li Baosheng, Yang Zihuo, Qian Shusheng, Meng Yabo, Shi Bohang, Ge Gongzhen, Ge Xianglan, Lu Yuheng, Xiao Zixiang, Zhou Shaoyuan, Xie Yisong, Qian Baoyuan, and Ms. Ge Shao Yi, Ms. Yuan Suzhen, and dozens of others. At the meeting, the compatriots reported the private information they had obtained, and it was resolved to organize a committee. Xia Hucen, Li Baosheng, Yang Zihuo, Qian Shusheng, Shi Bohang, Lu Yuheng, and Ge Gongzhen were publicly elected as committee members to contact various charitable organizations and request that the legal groups in Beijing and the countryside report on the disaster situation and send donation lists at any time, and actively raise funds separately. The meeting adjourned until late at night.

Anhui Compatriots Organize Flood Relief Association

The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, due to the severe flood disaster in their province, specially convened an emergency meeting of directors and supervisors yesterday. Those who attended included Xu Shiying, Li Weihou, Li Cishan, Guan Yunong, Xu Jingren, Wang Yuchen, Liu Zuwang, Li Zhenya, and fifty other people. Xu Jingren was publicly elected as chairman, and he reported that the disaster situation in the province was particularly serious compared to other provinces in the country. Forty-one counties have sent letters and telegrams requesting relief. He asked fellow-provincials to rise up quickly to provide relief in order to save the dying disaster victims. The discussion on the measures was very detailed, as were other cases. The resolutions were as follows: (1) In accordance with the provisions of Article 18 of the Association’s Articles of Association regarding special organizations, the Anhui Flood Relief Association in Shanghai was established. (2) The relief measures are divided into three steps: emergency relief, work relief, and disaster prevention. The association should actively raise funds, first release emergency relief, and make suggestions to the government on the second and third items for effective implementation. (3) All directors and supervisors will be members of the association, and fellow-provincial organizations in Shanghai will be asked to recommend three to five representatives or those with prestige in their hometowns to participate as members to expand the organization. A general meeting will be held on August 16 to elect a director in charge of standing affairs. (4) Since the fields and houses in various counties have been completely washed away, another telegram will be sent to the National Government and the Provincial Government requesting the immediate suspension of the Weiwei field donations to comfort the survivors. (5) A telegram will be sent to the Relief Committee requesting that 2 million yuan be allocated from the salt surplus treasury bills for emergency relief in Anhui Province as soon as possible to save the dying disaster victims in forty counties. (6) Please ask the Flood Relief Associations of Shanghai and various charitable organizations to provide immediate relief. (7) Formulate investigation forms and send them to various counties to fill in the disaster situation for future reference. (8) The Anhui Secondary School Joint Association opposes He Lu, who is not trustworthy, as the president of Anhui University. A telegram will be sent to the Provincial Government requesting a suitable successor from Anhui. (9) Wuyuan County sent a letter reporting that bandits were rampant. Please provide assistance. A telegram was sent to the Provincial Government requesting that troops be sent to suppress them. (10) Each captain of the fourth requisition should quickly collect the register and set a date for a captains' meeting to compare scores. (11) Li Weihou reported on contacting Li Bolao regarding the situation of the Anhui Hall and hoped to use it for permanent public welfare purposes. (12) The Anhui Provincial Department of Civil Affairs and Finance replied that the case of reducing the surtax in Guichi County has been forwarded to the county for investigation. A telegram was sent to the Anhui Provincial Government, stating: To Chairman Chen of the Anhui Provincial Government, the representatives of various counties in northern Anhui requested exemption from the Weitian donation. The association has previously reported the Gengdai telegram, which detailed the proof of the ownership of Weitian by the people and the determination of property rights. Please cancel the levy to relieve the people's difficulties and invite inspection and verification. Subsequently, the Ministry of Finance replied that it had telegraphed the Anhui Official Property Reclamation Bureau to verify and report for verification, etc. Now, the counties along the Yangtze River and Huai River in Anhui Province have all been turned into swamps. The fields and houses have been washed away, the tombs have become ruins, the people have been injured and killed, and saving the dead is not enough. How can we care about the Dingfu and the so-called Weitian donation that the officials are exhaustively searching for? Even if the flood recedes, the sea and the fields will change, and the people will be displaced. There will be no clothes or food, and the eyes will be full of desolation. Even if the government wants to impose harsh taxes, where can it find the difficult refugees who have fled the disaster and force them to pay fees? This is unbearable. It is hoped that the government will uphold the virtue of cherishing life and issue a clear order to permanently exempt this deformed donation, so that the people can recuperate and breathe a little. On behalf of the dying people in Anhui who have suffered from the disaster, we ask for your orders and hope that you will immediately abolish the collection agency and send a swift reply. The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai kowtows. Qing.

Hubei Native Association Held Disaster Relief Fundraising Meeting Yesterday

Disaster Area Spans Over Forty Counties

Millions of Disaster Victims

The Hubei Native Association in Shanghai has been receiving telegrams from the Hubei Provincial Government's Hubei Flood Disaster Relief Committee for days, and especially held an emergency meeting at its association's location on South Wuxi Road yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Over thirty people attended, including Liu Renshi, Han Yongqing, Luo Buzhou, Liu Wanqing, Sun Songnian, Du Baiqing, Wang Shuicheng, Wang Xiaozhai, Xiao Shouzhi, Ming Runshen, Gao Jianqing, Yi Nanzhen, Yu Yanqing, Chang Caichen, Lu Xingjie, Zhang Jitang, Wang Shutang, Wang Quanwang, Cao Dongchuan, Liu Taichen, and Zhang Shutang. Sun Songnian was publicly elected as acting chairman, and Ouyang Shenzhai as recorder. After the formalities were observed, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and read the telegrams, roughly stating that since the beginning of summer, Hubei Province has been experiencing incessant rain, causing flash floods and submerging people, livestock, fields, and homes beyond calculation. The disaster area has now reached over forty counties, with over millions of disaster victims. In Wuhan alone, approximately two hundred thousand people are homeless and without food. Although the Disaster Relief Committee is trying to provide relief, it's like adding a cup of water to a cartload of burning firewood, and the future is long. If post-disaster planning is not addressed, there will be no survivors. It is hoped that everyone present will devise effective methods to provide rescue. Ming Runshen rose and said that since the disaster situation is so severe, a slight delay will render assistance ineffective. All the gentlemen present today are benevolent and enthusiastic about charity. He requested that everyone donate on the spot to the best of their ability. Gao Jianqing said that rescuing disaster victims is an immeasurable act of merit. Even a dollar is not too little, and ten thousand dollars is not too much. In short, donating one more dollar means saving one more life. He hoped for generous donations to save more disaster victims. The chairman immediately put the proposals of the two gentlemen to a vote, which was unanimously approved. Wang Shao Cheng took the lead in pledging two thousand yuan. Liu Wanqing, Liu Renshi, Kun Yongqing, and Luo Buzhou each pledged one thousand yuan. Wang Xiaozhai and Xiao Shouzhi each pledged six hundred yuan. Chang Caichen pledged five hundred yuan. Ming Runshen pledged four hundred yuan. Guan Jiongzhi pledged three hundred yuan. Sun Songnian, Er Baiqing, Gao Jianqing, Yi Nanzhen, and Lu Xingjie each pledged two hundred yuan. Cao Dongchuan, Wang Shutang, Yu Yanqing, Zhang Jitang, Liu Taichen, and Wang Quanwang each pledged one hundred yuan. It was publicly decided that the pledged donations would be delivered to the bank for deposit within three days to be remitted to Hubei first to address the immediate crisis. It was decided to organize the Hubei Native Association in Shanghai Flood Disaster Relief Fundraising Committee, and Liu Renshi, Liu Wanqing, Ming Runshen, Gao Jianqing, Yi Nanzhen, Lu Xingjie, and Zhang Jitang were publicly elected as working committee members. Du Baiqing and Sun Songnian were authorized to handle the donation collection and remittance matters. This was unanimously approved. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

French Concession Revises Corpse Examination Location

The Bureau of Public Works Hospital

Effective Today

The examination of corpses in cases of fatalities within the French Concession used to be handled during the time of the Mixed Court by detectives dispatched by the police station, who would transport the corpses to the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall examination office at the intersection of Ningbo Road and the East Water and Fire Street. Then, the Criminal Division or the Traffic Division of the General Patrol Bureau would report to the judge of the Mixed Court for an inspection. In cases of suspicious corpses that could not be immediately examined, Western doctors would be sent for a detailed examination, or the corpses would be transported by vehicle to the small infirmary of the hospital established by the Bureau of Public Works in Lujiawan for autopsy. Afterward, the doctors would issue an examination report to the Mixed Court for review. Now that the Mixed Court has been taken back by the Chinese government and the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Local Court have been established, the court has revised the procedures for corpse examination. The police station is instructed to transport the corpses by vehicle to the small infirmary of the Bureau of Public Works Hospital at the intersection of Qiqi Road and Xujiahui Road, and report to the court's prosecutor for examination in conjunction with a forensic doctor. The hospital has already notified the police station, and the new procedures will be implemented starting today.

Commemorative Service for Chiang Wei-shui Scheduled

The Preparatory Office for the Memorial Service for Mr. Chiang Wei-shui, a pioneer of the Taiwan People's Liberation Movement, announced that Mr. Chiang Wei-shui of Taiwan led the Taiwanese people in revolutionary movements for nearly twenty years, with the aim of seeking freedom and equality for the people. All comrades, both domestic and foreign, who support the revolution, will undoubtedly share in this deep sorrow. Therefore, we have decided to hold a memorial service for Mr. Chiang on the morning of the 14th of this month at 9:00 AM at the Southeast Medical College in the Shanghai Military Camp in the South City of Shanghai. We sincerely hope that all our compatriots, comrades, and various organizations and institutions will honor us with their presence or send representatives to participate in the memorial service to comfort the pioneer and encourage those who follow. This is our sincere prayer. August 8th, the 20th year of the Republic of China. Please send condolences to the Preparatory Office, No. 133 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, telephone 19151, Overseas Chinese Hospital.

Business Tax Still Levied on Off-Site Wholesale Outlets

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday stating that business tax should still be levied on off-site wholesale outlets, and forwarded the letter to the Science Instrument Hall. The direct reply, dated July 15, stated that it had received a letter stating that if manufactured goods have left the manufacturing site and are sold in established sales outlets, please exempt them from additional sales business tax. The association immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for instructions. Now, the Ministry's Jiang Dai Dian Fu letter No. 6752 states: "The deletion of the telegraph is noted. According to Article 1 of the Business Tax Law, the nature of the business tax is that it is collected from businesses operating in cities within various provinces and does not adhere to the principle of one tax per item. For the convenience of both tax collection and tax payment, the Ministry has issued five interpretation methods for various provincial governments to follow. Previously, the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments submitted the business tax rate table for manufacturing industries, and the Qingdao municipal government submitted the business tax regulations to the Ministry. After detailed review and approval, these were submitted to the Executive Yuan for filing. According to the previous telegram, it should still be handled in accordance with the Ministry's Fu letter No. 5675. The manufacturing industry business tax rate tables for Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and the Qingdao Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations are enclosed for reference. Please forward these to the relevant parties for their information." It was noted that Article 12 of the Qingdao Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations stipulates that if the manufacturing industry directly sells its manufactured goods at its manufacturing location, regardless of whether it is wholesale or retail, only the manufacturing industry's business tax is levied, and the sales industry's business tax is not levied. However, if it leaves the manufacturing location and establishes another location for sales, regardless of whether it is the same factory owner or the same brand as the original manufacturing plant, the sales industry's business tax is levied, and the manufacturing industry's business tax is not levied. In addition to the various tables and examples, which the association will not attach separately, we are hereby forwarding the telegram for your information.

Record of the County Party and Government Dialogue Meeting

27th Meeting

The Shanghai County Party Headquarters convened the 27th Party and Government Dialogue Meeting yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. Peng Liren, Lü Zhe, and Kang Qiang from the County Party Headquarters, County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, Director of the Finance Bureau Wang Huazhao, Director of the Construction Bureau Sun Shengzeng, Zhu Jinxun (acting), and Director of Education Shi She attended. Peng Liren chaired the meeting and reported on the following matters: Matters for discussion: (1) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, submitted by the Third County Congress, to urge the county government to issue a notice to all districts strictly prohibiting opium and gambling cases. The result was that the District Party Headquarters and District Public Office will be responsible for investigation, and a secret report will be submitted every half month. The county government will strictly enforce the ban based on the report and report the enforcement results to the County Party Headquarters. (2) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, submitted by the Third County Congress, to liberally issue education funds to promote education. The result was to follow the original plan: (A) The Finance Bureau will handle the collection of land and house deed taxes. (B) The Education Bureau will formulate a plan to use temple property to fund education. (C) A proposal will be submitted to the Second Provincial Congress to suggest that the Ministry of Finance allocate additional salt tax revenue to fund education. (3) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, submitted by the County Congress, on how to improve agricultural irrigation. The result was to have the county government forward the proposal to the Water Conservancy Department and raise funds within the local budget for implementation. (4) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, submitted by the County Congress, to promote telephone service in all townships and towns in the county. The result was that the Construction Bureau is already planning to complete this in the short term. (5) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, submitted by the County Congress, to promote farm household side businesses. The result was to promote chicken farming, and Shi She, Wang Huazhao, and Lü Zhe will draft detailed plans to be discussed at the next dialogue meeting. (6) Proposal by the County Executive Committee, regarding the (organization of the Shanghai County Consumer Cooperative). The result was to have the (organization) printed and distributed to various agencies for their opinions, to be discussed at the next congress. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Various Groups

Concern for the Xin Kang Shipwreck Case

Bereaved Families Convene Emergency Meeting

Regarding the case of the bereaved families of the Xin Kang shipwreck suing the Japanese Mail Steamship Company for damages, the Shanghai Special District Court has scheduled a hearing for the 15th of this month at 8:00 AM in the Ninth Tribunal to summon both the plaintiff and defendant for questioning. The bereaved families feel that after two years, there has been no progress in the aftermath, and the physical and mental suffering they have endured is indescribable. Fortunately, two prominent lawyers, Wu Jingxiong and Sheng Zhenwei, have taken on the case as pro bono representatives, prioritizing national rights and the people's lives. The Special District Court will soon commence the trial, marking a small milestone in this case. In the future, all issues related to comforting the deceased and providing for the living will depend on the court's impartial judgment and strict enforcement. At the same time, the support of the entire nation is needed to force the Japanese to comply. The bereaved families in Shanghai have scheduled an emergency meeting for the afternoon of the 12th at 1:00 PM to discuss the next steps. It is reported that various industrial, commercial, and academic groups in Shanghai are paying close attention to this case, and representatives will be sent to observe the court hearing when it commences.

Local News

Asia

The First Stage of the Walking Tour is Completed

Received Hospitality Along the Way

Fatigue, Treatment in Shanghai

The Chinese Youth Asia Walking Tour, consisting of Li Mengsheng, Hu Sujuan, and Du Jingxiong, who joined in Annam, has completed its first stage of the journey and returned to Shanghai from Singapore. They are currently staying at Qi's residence at 42 Shunda Lane, Keming Road. The group departed from the North Railway Station on June 28th of the 19th year of the Republic. They traveled through Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong, and then through Annam, Siam, the Malay Peninsula, Singapore, etc. They were welcomed by people from all walks of life, and the French government of Annam also took responsibility for protecting them. Therefore, they were able to investigate the rural life and organization of various ethnic groups along the way, and focus on the primitive life of uncivilized humans, as well as collect unique utensils, texts, etc. When passing through Cambodia, they met with the king and received from the king a badge and three Buddha statues. Upon arriving in Siam, they were monitored by the police. When they reached the Siamese capital, they negotiated with the government to obtain freedom of movement within the country. Later, the Siamese press, business, and political circles jointly held a meeting to welcome them and actively promoted the event in the newspapers. Therefore, the group attracted considerable attention in Siam. Singapore marked the end of the first stage of their journey. Due to the long journey and inconsistent water and soil conditions, they contracted stomach problems. Therefore, they temporarily returned to Shanghai for treatment and to complete the first phase. When the group left Singapore, various newspapers, the Lizhi Society, and various schools went to the dock to see them off, creating a lively scene.

Recent Photo of Ms. Hu Sujuan

Public Concession

Two Parks, East and West, to Be Built

And a Children's Playground to Be Built Separately

The Shanghai Times reported that the Bureau of Public Works Engineering Office recently purchased 40 mu of land near its existing property on Singapore Road in the Western District to be developed into a park. The land price is between 15,000 and 16,000 taels per mu. The land is bordered by Jiaozhou Road to the east, the Zhabei boundary to the north, and roads on the southwest sides. The layout of the park is planned to imitate the layout of Huishan Park. Construction will begin soon, and it is expected to be completed by next summer. The existing 25 mu of land on Singapore Road, currently used as a children's park, will be redeveloped into a school for the expansion of Chinese education. In the Eastern District, a piece of land is also being negotiated for the construction of a park to meet the needs of Eastern District residents. In addition, the flower room west of the Waibaidu Bridge in the Central District has been demolished and converted into a children's playground.

Western Woman Attempts Suicide

Apparently Due to Disappointment in Love

Miss K.W. Allan, a Western woman in her twenties, has been living in China for many years, working as a typist at various foreign firms. She has been residing in Room C, 4th Floor, 762 Avenue Joffre, French Concession, for almost three years, paying 96 taels of rent per month. She goes out early and returns late, employing one female maid and one male servant. Yesterday evening, at around 6:00 PM, she returned to her residence, appearing very depressed. She then ordered the maid to go out and closed the door. Until 8:20 PM, the maid noticed that the door had been closed for a long time and had not been opened, which aroused her suspicions. She knocked on the door repeatedly, but there was no response. Helpless, the maid rushed to inform her relatives, who used an axe to break open the door. They found Allan lying stiffly on the bed, her face pale, and she had already lost consciousness. An empty medicine bottle was left on the table, indicating that she had attempted suicide by taking poison. She was rushed to Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road for treatment. The reporter initially heard that a Russian had committed suicide by shooting himself at 652 Avenue Joffre. Upon arriving at 762, the truth was revealed. According to the doorman, the lady usually looked like a Chinese person when she went in and out and had many friends. It is said that she initially had a lover, but they broke up shortly after. Recently, she met another lover, and they had a close relationship. Now, she suddenly attempted suicide, and it is suspected that she was mostly heartbroken.

Wife Commits Suicide Due to Husband's Affair

Yu Gu's Situation is Particularly Pitiful

Yu Gu, a local housewife and wife of the owner of the Youhua Automobile Company in the South City Military Camp, was 18 years old. Because her husband recently had an affair and often did not return home day and night, she found out about it. Last night, after her husband returned, they had a major falling out. Afterward, she was extremely resentful and secretly swallowed raw opium to commit suicide. She was discovered and sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. She died at 11:00 AM the next morning. The hospital notified her family to make arrangements to take the body back for the funeral.

Jia Linmei Requests

Divorce From a Gluttonous and Lazy Husband

Jia Linmei, a local young woman residing at 72 East of the Lingjia Wooden Bridge in Yangjing, Pudong, is 25 years old this year. When she was 17 years old, she married Zhao Asi. The relationship between the couple was poor, and they were estranged, so she returned to her mother's house in and has been supporting herself by doing needlework. It has been two years since then. Now, Jia Linmei has hired lawyer Wang Chengkuan to file a petition for mediation for divorce with the local court, but it was unsuccessful. Therefore, she has filed a formal lawsuit. The case was heard in court by Judge Wei Weiqing. Jia Linmei stated that because the defendant is gluttonous and lazy, he has sold all the furniture and dowry at home to buy opium to smoke. She could not live like this any longer and requested a divorce. The defendant, Zhao Asi, stated that he is 30 years old, a local, and currently works at Zhao Yongxing Gold Thread Shop at 45 Xue Lane. He does not want a divorce. The judge ordered both parties to invite their parents to court for the next hearing for further interrogation.

The Reason for Two Widows Evicting a Guest

Wang Youxiu Still Knows About Human Shame, Right?

Wang Jinwen, the son of Wang Ni, a widow from the Zhujiaqiao Township in Pudong, worked as a clerk at the Mobil Oil Station. He married Xi. He was 24 years old. Several months after the marriage, Wang Jinwen died. After his father cried in pain, he died within two weeks. Two generations of widows worked hard to make a living, living a simple life. The neighbors praised them. It has been over three years. A tenant, Wang Youxiu, because he had no wife, volunteered to be Xi's second husband. Wang Ni and Wang Xi were unwilling. Wang Youxiu, without any sense of shame, kept trying to seduce her, causing Wang Ni and others to evict him. Wang refused to move out, so the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law threw Wang's belongings out. Wang then filed a complaint with the Third District Fifth Precinct, accusing them of robbery. After questioning, they were arrested and transferred to the local court for interrogation.

Seducing a Pregnant Woman and Forcing an Abortion

Xie Zhihong and Others Extremely Unlawful

Ren Jiaorong of Minde Road, Zhabei, and his wife, Ren Zhang, brought Xie Zhihong, Fang Keshan, Jin Bingxi, and others to the No. 2 Branch of the Fourth District police station, accusing Xie of seducing the woman last year, instigating her to divorce Ren, and taking 200 yuan of Ren's subsidy. However, the woman was five months pregnant and was forced to have an abortion. The woman suffered all kinds of pain and realized she had encountered a criminal. She has reconciled with her husband as before. Unexpectedly, Xie wanted to extort 500 yuan and went with Fang Keshan, Jin Bingxi, and others to threaten her, so they brought them to justice. Xie and others absolutely denied the accusations, saying that they were baffled by the reason for their arrest. The station chief believed that Xie had committed seduction, extortion, and all kinds of extremely unlawful acts, so he sent them to the local court for investigation yesterday.

Yu Gu Died with Blood Flowing from Seven Orifices

Yu Yuqi, a native of Ningbo, was 22 years old and worked as a worker in the Qiu Xin Machine Factory in the South Bund. He lived upstairs in Youhua Automobile Shop No. 1562 in the Shanghai Military Camp. His wife, Gu, was 18 years old. They had been married for just over a year. Yesterday morning, at about 5 a.m., Gu was still lying in bed when her face suddenly turned pale and she did not say a word. Her family noticed and immediately took her to a nearby hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was said that she had suffered an attack from smoking opium. Because it had been too long, it was impossible to save her, and she died soon after. When Gu died, blood flowed from her seven orifices, which was a tragic sight. The chief of the First Branch of the First District heard about the incident and, considering it a matter of life and death, immediately ordered Qin Defang, the local head of the 23rd subdistrict, to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy.

Young Girl Falls from Balcony

Life Cannot Be Guaranteed

A 14-year-old girl from the Ding family at No. 1974 Hua'an Fang (Chinese area), North Zhejiang Road, went to the balcony upstairs to collect clothes at about 4 p.m. yesterday (the 9th). She was careless and fell from the edge of the balcony, immediately losing consciousness. Her family immediately took her to the nearby Gongyi Hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was found that she had suffered severe internal injuries and her life could not be guaranteed.

The Son of a Bandit is Always a Bandit

Zheng Ming Arrested; Changshu Requests Extradition

Zheng Yushan, the famous pirate leader, had many followers and specialized in robbery and kidnapping, committing all kinds of evil deeds. The Changshu County Government sent detectives to Shanghai to arrest Zheng and send him to Changshu, where he was interrogated and executed by firing squad. Unexpectedly, his son, Zheng Ming, served as the commander in his father's bandit gang, rampaging through the countryside, robbing, killing, and kidnapping. Since his father's execution, he has gathered his followers and disturbed the areas of Fushan and Baimao, claiming to avenge his father. Coastal residents find it difficult to sleep peacefully. Zheng Ming came to Shanghai to replenish military supplies a few days ago, and the detectives of the Xinzha Patrol Station in the Public Concession learned that Zheng was hiding in Zhabei. They immediately joined forces with the security corps to arrest Zheng and found a Browning pistol. He was detained in the patrol station. The Director of the Changshu Public Security Bureau heard the news and yesterday prepared a document, dispatched four detectives and eight armed police officers with box cannons to Shanghai to prepare for his extradition for interrogation.

Old Man Chopped

Yesterday morning, a Henan man, Wen Shijin, was chopped on the way and sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that the incident occurred near Ma Lishi. The assailant was about sixty years old and used to be a monk. Most of the injuries were on the head, about six or seven cuts. He lost consciousness due to excessive bleeding after arriving at the hospital.

Opium Found on Jiangbei Boat

Wang Songshan, the police chief of the Yujidun Police Station of the Second Detachment of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, led his team members Lu Dianxiang and others to patrol the river near Yujidun at about 11 a.m. yesterday. They saw a Jiangbei boat approaching and immediately went forward to carry out an inspection. They found a net basket in the cabin, containing a small tin box. When they tried to insert an iron bar into the small tin box, they suddenly felt a wooden board blocking them. When they tried harder and pierced through the partition, they smelled a strange smell, which aroused their suspicion. They then tried to open the box and found ten packages of opium, weighing about 120 taels. They took the boat owner, Zhou Zhenbiao, and the evidence back to the station and transferred them to the South City Headquarters. During the preliminary trial by Chief Xu, Zhou Zhenbiao confessed that he was 64 years old, from Huai'an, and made a living by driving a boat. The iron box was entrusted to him by a guest, Liu Xuepu, to take to Yancheng, and he had already gone there to wait. However, he did not know that there was opium hidden inside. The boatman was charged with carrying contraband and ordered to prepare a document to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The Central Police Station Arrested Two Thieves

Liu Shaokui, the chief Chinese detective of the Central Police Station's General Investigation Department, learned that bandits were hiding in Room 15 of the Kaitai Hotel on Hubei Road. He and Chinese detectives Feng Zhiming, Wang Chengying, and others secretly went to the address at 9:45 p.m. a few days ago, and arrested Kang Dechang, a native of Chongming. They seized two fake pistols and took him to the police station. Under questioning, they learned that his accomplice, Huang Amao, a native of Nanhui, was hiding at No. 1034 Dong Hanbi Road. The detectives went again and arrested Huang. The next day, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District. The police lawyer, Ru Bao Yi, explained the case and said that the police had not yet investigated the case and requested an extension. Kang Dechang confessed that in November of last year, he and Huang Amao and Gu A'er, Zhang A'er, who have already been punished, went to a certain cigarette paper shop on Dong Youheng Road and a certain cake shop on Yangshupu Road to rob, using the seized fake pistols. Huang Amao completely denied the charges. Judge Zhou Hanting reviewed the confessions and ordered them to be detained separately, pending further interrogation at a later date.

Car Crashes into a Big Tree

Driver Careless, Driver Seriously Injured

One Passenger Also Injured

A rental car No. 17606 of the Gordan Road Republican Automobile Company was carrying four passengers, one male and three female, yesterday afternoon. The driver, Weng Huisheng, was driving to Wusong for a trip. When he arrived near Zhanghuabang on Jungong Road, he saw a car parked on the side of the road slowly driving. The driver swerved, intending to overtake the car in front. Unexpectedly, he was careless and crashed into a large tree on the side of the road, causing the car body to be violently shaken. The driver was seriously injured and shards of glass were embedded in his neck. One of the passengers, a woman named Tao Yan, was injured, and the others were fortunate to be unharmed. The car in front stopped when it saw the situation. The car, driven by a Westerner, with black license plate number 11781, had two Westerners jump out and help the injured driver and woman Tao Yan into the car and take them to the Haibin Public Hospital on Wusong Wai Ma Road for treatment.

Stealing More Than Forty Boxes of Flower Bricks

Tang A'gen, a bricklayer from Pudong, colluded with a gang on the evening of the 18th of last month to steal more than forty boxes of very valuable flower bricks from the factory of the British Kangyi Foreign Company on Gaoen Road in the French Concession. They sold the stolen goods and shared the money. The owner reported the theft to the police and asked them to investigate. Chen Yisan, a detective from the French Concession, learned of the case, arrested Tang, and found the original stolen goods in the Public Concession and the Chinese area, and took him to the police station. The next day, he was sent to the Criminal Court of the Second Special District for investigation. First, the police lawyer Chen Ming explained the case. Tang confessed that he was invited by two people nicknamed Deaf Barrel and Little Songjiang to go together. The civilians were on the lookout outside, and the two of them went inside to steal the bricks. He did not know where the two of them were now. Judge Xiong Huihua reviewed the confession and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further interrogation on August 15.

New Shipping Route Opened in Tongzhou Waterway

Announcement No. 1009 of the Marine Affairs Department of the Customs: This Marine Affairs Department has checked the newly opened shipping route in the Tongzhou waterway within the boundary of the Jianghai Customs, and stopped the current shipping route. It has also moved and canceled the police floats according to the situation. The details are listed on the left. Due to the change in the situation of the Tongzhou waterway in the Yangtze River, the current waterway is stopped, and a new waterway is opened to the north of the current waterway, with floats placed to facilitate navigation. The situation is listed below and will be implemented around August 11 of this year. No further notice will be given at that time. The Xu Liujingzui float will be moved to the new location, with the Xu Liujingzui pile bearing south 3 degrees and 3/4 west, 1.72 nautical miles away. The float will be changed from red to black. The east float will be moved to the new location, with the Xu Liujingzui pile bearing south 39 degrees and 1/4 east, 5.21 nautical miles away. The other conditions remain the same. The dangerous float (translation) will be moved to the new location, with the Langshan Pagoda bearing north 1 degree and 3/4 east, 6.17 nautical miles away. The other conditions remain the same. The rotating float (translation) will be moved to the new location, with the Langshan Pagoda bearing north 9 degrees and 3/4 east, 5.69 nautical miles away. The other conditions remain the same. The central float, west float, and north entrance float will be canceled when the new waterway is opened. All the degrees listed above are based on the compass direction, refer to the Chinese Navy's nautical chart No. 142 for clarity. It is hereby announced for all ships to comply and be careful to remember, so as to avoid negligence. Xi Liman, Director of the Marine Affairs Department, August 1, 20th year of the Republic of China
